  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_350e4462-15fe-4dac-9177-e0e072d0b933'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText9018271622695640854" style="display:none">Mortals rule the desert nation of Miraji, but mythical beasts still roam the wild and remote areas, and rumor has it that somewhere, djinn still perform their magic.  For humans, it’s an unforgiving place, especially if you’re poor, orphaned, or female.<br /><br />Amani Al’Hiza is all three. She’s a gifted gunslinger with perfect aim, but she can’t shoot her way out of Dustwalk, the back-country town where she’s destined to wind up wed or dead.<br /><br />Then she meets Jin, a rakish foreigner, in a shooting contest, and sees him as the perfect escape route. But though she’s spent years dreaming of leaving Dustwalk, she never imagined she’d gallop away on mythical horse—or that it would take a foreign fugitive to show her the heart of the desert she thought she knew.<br /><br /><i>Rebel of the Sands</i> reveals what happens when a dream deferred explodes—in the fires of rebellion, of romantic passion, and the all-consuming inferno of a girl finally, at long last, embracing her power.</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/664938-i-have-just-finished-this-amazing-book-and">I have just finished this amazing book and I am bereft. Is there anything at all like this out there ? I also loved Truthwitch and I am a massive fan of Kristen Cashore. So I am looking for a story with a smart female protagonist, set in a fantasy world with adventure, magic and romance. So what should I read next?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_664938'><a id="like_count_community_question_664938" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/664938?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">19 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F24934065-rebel-of-the-sands">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/17890654-amada"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1444979146i/17890654._UY100_CR1,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/17890654-amada">Amada</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The Throne of Glass series by Sarah J Maas is SERIOUSLY AMAZING. It is definitely worth all the hype, I promise. Each book gets better and better. So <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The Throne of Glass series by Sarah J Maas is SERIOUSLY AMAZING. It is definitely worth all the hype, I promise. Each book gets better and better. So if the first one starts off "flatter" than you expected...just keep on going!!!!! YOU WON'T REGRET IT. <br /><br />*Also, the other series by Sarah J Mass, A Court of Thorns and Roses is a must read! The second book in this series, A Court of Mist and Fury is my favorite book I have ever read! And it just won the award for "Best Young Adult Fantasy"!!!!!! SOOOO GOOD!<br /><br />And lastly, if you haven't read the Wrath and the Dawn, this book is truly beautiful. It is easily my second favorite book. It has an amazing lead female protagonist who is smart and witty, it has adventure, and the romance is utterly beautiful. Although technically fantasy, I would not read this purely for the fantasy theme. But read, fall in love, and enjoy the beautiful adventure it will take you on. <br /><br />I hope you enjoy these series as much as I have &lt;3<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_1428502644" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1428502644" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1428502644?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1428502644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14594448502724159277"><blockquote>
  <i>Jin had the sort of smile that would turn over whole empires to the enemy - that made me feel like suddenly I understood him exactly, even though I knew nothing about him.</i>
</blockquote><br/>I was so certain I would love this book. A Middle-Eastern fantasy with djinn, magic and mythical horses? It's like a unique and delicious recipe for exactly the kind of book I would love. And yet, for the first two thirds, I was so painfully bored I very nearly DNFed it.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24934065.Rebel_of_the_Sands__Rebel_of_the_Sands___1_' title='Rebel of the Sands (Rebel of the Sands, #1) by Alwyn Hamilton' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rebel of the Sands</a> does pick up toward the end when th</span>
  <span id="freeText14594448502724159277" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Jin had the sort of smile that would turn over whole empires to the enemy - that made me feel like suddenly I understood him exactly, even though I knew nothing about him.</i>
</blockquote><br />I was so certain I would love this book. A Middle-Eastern fantasy with djinn, magic and mythical horses? It's like a unique and delicious recipe for exactly the kind of book I would love. And yet, for the first two thirds, I was so painfully bored I very nearly DNFed it.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24934065.Rebel_of_the_Sands__Rebel_of_the_Sands___1_" title="Rebel of the Sands (Rebel of the Sands, #1) by Alwyn Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Rebel of the Sands</a> does pick up toward the end when the real fantasy and magic elements are finally introduced to the story. It takes a very long time to get there, though, and the journey is a slow one.<br /><br />I'm willing to admit that part of my problem with this book is a personal one. On two levels. <br /><br />1) Firstly, I just did not like the fusion of Arabian mythology with a Western setting. By "Western", I mean cowboys, shoot outs, saloons, etc. I didn't think it worked and, if you ask me, it succeeded in taking an area of the world that is oft-unexplored in modern fantasy and westernizing it.<br /><br />2) For the most part, this book mirrors the plot of the stream of other Westerns we've seen lately. Maybe I would have liked it more had I not already read the first two thirds in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17564519.Walk_on_Earth_a_Stranger__The_Gold_Seer_Trilogy___1_" title="Walk on Earth a Stranger (The Gold Seer Trilogy, #1) by Rae Carson" rel="nofollow noopener">Walk on Earth a Stranger</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23719270.Vengeance_Road" title="Vengeance Road by Erin Bowman" rel="nofollow noopener">Vengeance Road</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22501055.Under_a_Painted_Sky" title="Under a Painted Sky by Stacey Lee" rel="nofollow noopener">Under a Painted Sky</a>. <br /><br />My initial excitement over this return to the Western genre is petering out, because it seems that everyone is telling the same story. Badass, gun-toting heroine who, though pretty cool, is exactly the same in each book. Absent or dead parents forcing heroine to impersonate a cowboy and go on the road. Long-ass road trips, usually with accompanying hot dude.<br /><br />^This sums up the plot of each book I mentioned, as well as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24934065.Rebel_of_the_Sands__Rebel_of_the_Sands___1_" title="Rebel of the Sands (Rebel of the Sands, #1) by Alwyn Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Rebel of the Sands</a>. And yes, I'll admit the other books may just have the advantage of being first but, for whatever reason, they were so much more compelling than this one.<br /><br />The beginning is literally all about getting Amani and Jin on the road together. Jin is an easy-to-spot love interest as early as page seven, when he is introduced with a detailed description of his bone structure *rolls eyes*, but the two have <b>zero chemistry</b>. Because Amani has been desperate to leave her town and Jin is a wanted fugitive, the two hit the road in a blaze of drama.<br /><br />I think what this story lacks for a long time is an end goal. I'm not a big fan of journey books, for a start, but it is even worse when I have no clue what we're moving towards, or what we should be concerned about. The bigger story emerges later, but by then I was bored and tired of reading about Amani and Jin riding around together and almost making out.<br /><br />I have no interest in the sequel.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14594448502724159277" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1532614863" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1532614863" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31923026-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533734143p2/31923026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1532614863?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/31923026-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1532614863" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16053964792910337908">Let me start by saying I don’t give out 5 stars easily. It has to be a book I find nothing wrong with, absolutely love, and plan on reading again and again. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24934065.Rebel_of_the_Sands__Rebel_of_the_Sands___1_' title='Rebel of the Sands (Rebel of the Sands, #1) by Alwyn Hamilton' rel='nofollow noopener'> Rebel of the Sands</a> does all of that. About halfway through I was freaking out because I wanted a sequel so badly. I knew I would need way more of this world and the characters. I seriously cannot recommend this book enough.<br/><br/>The story starts with a shooting competition. Amani is disguised as a boy and needs to win in order to finally have eno</span>
  <span id="freeText16053964792910337908" style="display:none">Let me start by saying I don’t give out 5 stars easily. It has to be a book I find nothing wrong with, absolutely love, and plan on reading again and again. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24934065.Rebel_of_the_Sands__Rebel_of_the_Sands___1_" title="Rebel of the Sands (Rebel of the Sands, #1) by Alwyn Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener"> Rebel of the Sands</a> does all of that. About halfway through I was freaking out because I wanted a sequel so badly. I knew I would need way more of this world and the characters. I seriously cannot recommend this book enough.<br /><br />The story starts with a shooting competition. Amani is disguised as a boy and needs to win in order to finally have enough money to escape Dustwalk and travel all the way to Izman, the place her mother always told stories about. It was said to be a place where a girl could be free and make her own choices. Her mother died almost a year ago leaving Amani to live with her aunt and uncle. They are awful. Her uncle wants to marry her off so he no longer has to take care of her, but is debating marrying her himself. Dustwalk is clearly a dead-end town for a girl. It make sense that she would rather die trying to escape the town. Amani meets a mysterious foreigner who appears to bring the perfect opportunity for her to finally leave. She has no clue her world is about to be changed forever.<br /><br />Amani is a very tough, feisty badass chick. She has attitude and a smart mouth, but is determined, strong, and compassionate. She is also incredible with a gun - quite the sharp shooter. She’s actually my favorite heroine in a ya book in quite some time.<br /><br />Every single chapter ended with something that kept me needing to read. If I could have, I wouldn’t have ever put the book down. The writing is completely engaging, while the world-building is original and exciting. The desert nation of Miraji has stories that read like folktales with all this mythology seeped in. This is where the fantasy genre comes into play. There is magic and immortal creatures like skinwalkers and nightmares that roam the desert. There is also a rebellion with a rebel prince plotting to take back his rightful throne.<br /><br />There is a whole lot going on, but it all flows together nicely. I enjoyed meeting all of the characters within the story. There aren’t too many to remember, but you definitely meet plenty throughout. I am excited to see where the story goes in the second book. I felt like Rebel of the Sands ended nicely without any crazy cliffhangers, but still left you wanting to read more. There was a nice slow-burning romance that actually felt real the way it developed. The chemistry at one point had me swooning. That just doesn’t happen with me, so consider me hooked. I cannot wait to see where it all goes.<br /><br />This western twist on an arabic-inspired setting works perfectly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16053964792910337908" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1203587405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7674296025226687582"><b>4.5 stars</b> Guys, meet your new favorite historical fantasy series. <br/><br/>This book has spectacular world-building, nimble dialogue, finely drawn characters, and epic battles with magic--not to mention so much chemistry between the main characters that the air is practically charged with the irresistible pull between them. <br/><br/>This is that sweeping story (and romance) you might've wanted from THE WRATH AND THE DAWN but didn't quite get. I loved the writing, I loved the characters, and I loved that everyone </span>
  <span id="freeText7674296025226687582" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b> Guys, meet your new favorite historical fantasy series. <br /><br />This book has spectacular world-building, nimble dialogue, finely drawn characters, and epic battles with magic--not to mention so much chemistry between the main characters that the air is practically charged with the irresistible pull between them. <br /><br />This is that sweeping story (and romance) you might've wanted from THE WRATH AND THE DAWN but didn't quite get. I loved the writing, I loved the characters, and I loved that everyone here, good or bad, believed in something bigger than themselves. I hope like hell this makes a lot of bestseller lists. It deserves it. <br /><br />And holy hell, it's a debut! So excited for more books from this author, and for this story to continue. <br /><br />More of a review to come.</span>

It was such a different take on anything I have read. We have Amani who is dead on with a gun and she's wanting to get out of her town and away from her evil uncle and his wives and kids. She's trying to make money to get the hell out of dodge. She ends up meeting a newcomer named, Jin. They eventually team up and hit the road. Although, it takes a bit for them to trust each other and what not. <br><br>Amani was lucky enough to capture a Buraqi which is a beautiful sand horse and if the person who touches it turns it into a real horse, it is theirs. Well of course, since women can't own a damn thing, Amani would have to give it to her sorry uncle. Anyhoo, things happen and Amani and Jin head out of town on said, Buraqi. <br><br><img alt=" " src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1499345971i/23220149.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I totally loved the world, the characters, the quests, pretty much everything.   <span id="freeText15363723792215011949" style="display:none"><blockquote> <b> "Tell me that and we’ll go. Right now. Save ourselves and leave this place to burn. Tell me that’s how you want your story to go and we’ll write it straight across the sand.” </b> </blockquote><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26047310.Rebel_of_the_Sands__Rebel_of_the_Sands___1_" title="Rebel of the Sands (Rebel of the Sands, #1) by Alwyn Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Rebel of the Sands</a> is one of the most delightful and thrilling books i've read in a long time. <b> this tiny, beautiful gem of a book is now one of my absolute favorites. </b> and i was left completely speechless after i’d finished it. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380432417ra/868583.gif" width="300" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>first off, i rarely mention this in reviews — but this book checks off all the boxes for aesthetics. the cover is so pretty just to look at -- all that glitter and sparkle and the BLUE AND GOLDEN COLORS. and i’ll be the first person to admit that i absolutely buy books by judging their covers occasionally (read: frequently).<br><br>we begin with one of the most riveting opening scenes i’ve read in a long time. the story begins with amani al’ hiza disguised as a boy, about to take part in a gun shooting competition. to escape Dustwalk, the dead-end desert town she lives in, she needs to win the prize money so that she can flee to Izman, the great capital city, where it’s said that a girl can be free and make her own choices. it’s essential that she gets the hell out, and quickly, because she discovered a few days before that her repulsive uncle wants to marry her (yikes). what amani isn’t counting on is the mysterious foreigner jin. fate intertwines their destinies when they become temporary allies at the competition. before long, amani finds herself traveling across the desert with jin while caught up in a tangled web of politics, rebellion, myth and romance.<br><br>amani was a breath of fresh air. she was a wonderful, gutsy, snarky heroine without being a mary sue; and i fell in love with her fiery personality very quickly.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382325175ra/5820612.gif" width="350" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>amani completely redefines badassery. she’s an amazing female lead who’s a wicked shot as well as sassy and smart. amani dreams of escaping her abusive relatives to carve out her own path in life and discover her own personal kind of awesome. she’s defying every stereotype about females in the book and crushing society’s sexism beneath her heel. and she’s fierce and brave and loyal and loving and doesn’t take nonsense from anyone! don’t get me wrong. amani’s definitely an imperfect heroine - she’s very reckless and makes mistakes. but even though she makes mistakes, she acknowledges them and learns from them and never makes them again. and this is what i call excellent character development.<br><br>another thing i really loved about this book is THE SETTING! <i> rebel of the sands </i> has a beautiful, carefully crafted plot woven with myths, ancient tales, desert fantasy, magic horses, rebel princes, and a touch of slow-burn romance. it’s just the perfect blend to leave you swooning and turning the pages for more. the story is told with an addictive simplicity, and yet the world building was so well done and the fantasy was absolutely epic. the mythology and ancient tales tied in so well with the direction of the plot and resulted in a tantalising sense of mystery that shadowed my reading throughout the book. also, the storyline is highly addictive and the first chapter hooked me in like never before, transporting me into a scene of action immediately. this continued throughout the entire book with every chapter ending in something that left me wanting to keep reading. i know this is a tiny book, with only 300+ pages but there was <i> so much </i> action packed into the pages and the best part is it didn’t even feel annoying or exaggerated because it was <i> so real. </i> i didn’t see half the plot coming, but it was so realistic and engaging and set the blood thrumming in my veins with anticipation. literally. i tried to read whenever i could spare free time during college hours because i just had to know what happens next. it left me on the edge of my seat, my heart pounding for the characters and rooting so hard for them. and then before i knew it, i’d flipped to the very last page and was left an awestruck mess, craving the sequel like a drug.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424973888ra/13825891.gif" width="1000" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1477196013i/20926666.gif" width="250" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>in the book, we’re brought to a desert country named Miraji, where mythical desert creatures rule the sands and a missing rebel prince is preparing to reclaim his throne. here's a quick guide to the desert's creatures taken from the official website:<br><br><blockquote> <i> Djinnis - One of God’s First Beings: men made of out of smokeless fire. The true rulers of the desert, their powers are both great and mysterious. Travellers are warned to not trespass on their domain or disturb them in the desert. And to always be polite to strangers lest they be a Djinni in disguise.<br>Buraqi - A horse fashioned out of sand and wind, the Buraqi run wild from one side of the desert to the other. They may appear as black as the sand of a cool desert night or as brilliant red as a bloody dawn over a sand dune.<br>Rocs - Great birds the size of palaces that can darken the sun with their wings.<br>Nightmares - A breed of Ghoul that remains in the sands like an infestation, coming out only at night. These creatures stalk sleeping on the wings of a bat, with the maw of a monster. They crouch on a man’s chest to inject him with venom that infects his mind and body, sending him into a terrible sleep.<br>Skinwalkers - If the Skinwalkers have a shape of their own it has long been forgotten, as they shift their form from that of one victim to another. A Skinwalker is known to devour the flesh of an unsuspecting desert traveller, and then assume his form to prey on the rest of his travelling party. </i> </blockquote><br><br>this tale is really a breath of fresh air in the YA fantasy genre, with its Middle-Eastern (Arabic? Persian?) desert setting and influences, and its intricate world-building that leaves you hooked and makes you feel like you’re in the fictional world itself. i’ve honestly not encountered such a well thought-out fantasy for a while. <br><br>romance is alluded to very subtly in the summary, and hinted at in the book, but it never takes up a major part of the book, and neither does it slow down the plot at all. i loved it even more purely for that reason. amani and jin start out as uncertain allies, except amani is adamant that doesn’t need a man and constantly tries to escape from jin because she doesn’t trust him. But then through a number of plot twists, they end up together again, traveling across the desert with a caravan, supposedly on an alternative route to Izman. i enjoyed watching their friendship so much, reading their snarky banter back and forth (amani! she’s such a queen of sass) and it definitely didn’t turn into a steamy romance at all. instead, alwyn hamilton chooses to focus more on the gripping action of the plot, while including some intense moments between amani and jin which hint at their budding romance. this makes the book so much more riveting, and the blossoming relationship between amani and jin very sneaky, but no less sweet. (they do share a kiss or two.) but even with their romance not being the main focus, <b> I STILL SHIP THESE TWO SO HARD, MY PRECIOUS CHILDREN. PLEASE LET ME PROTECT THEM AT ALL COSTS. </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450305175ra/17406255.gif" width="280" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>the ending of <i> rebel of the sands </i> was something else! a perfect balance of “I’M CRYING THIS WAS SO LOVELY” and “OMG GIVE ME MORE”. for now there isn’t a cliffhanger, but i’m pretty sure there will be one in the next book. but this was great, because at least i didn’t have to live in suspense for the next year! <br><br><i> rebel of the sands </i> is a fantastic debut, a book i loved to pieces after reading only a few pages. it’s a beautifully told young adult fantasy with characters that stay with you long after you’ve finished reading. i really fell in love with amani and jin and all the supporting characters and I NEED THE NEXT BOOK. NOW.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b> “The world makes things for each place. Fish for the sea, Rocs for the mountain skies, and girls with sun in their skin and perfect aim for a desert that doesn't let weakness live." </b>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="15363723792215011949" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1564326353" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1564326353" />
    <a title="Kiki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4074594-kiki"><img alt="Kiki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545082712p2/4074594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1564326353?book_show_action=true">Feb 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kiki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kiki" href="/user/show/4074594-kiki">Kiki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1564326353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7260029485757686042">This book was...really something. And by "something" I mean "bad." So bad I ended up leaving it behind in France even though the copy I had didn't belong to me. It's fine, though, because I'm pretty sure the person who the book belongs to would rather it were across the channel too.<br/><br/>I couldn't make head nor tail of it: it's a weird blend of the Wild West and bastardised Arabic folklore, set against a sort of steampunky backdrop with a low fantasy element and also a rebellion and this book just ne</span>
  <span id="freeText7260029485757686042" style="display:none">This book was...really something. And by "something" I mean "bad." So bad I ended up leaving it behind in France even though the copy I had didn't belong to me. It's fine, though, because I'm pretty sure the person who the book belongs to would rather it were across the channel too.<br /><br />I couldn't make head nor tail of it: it's a weird blend of the Wild West and bastardised Arabic folklore, set against a sort of steampunky backdrop with a low fantasy element and also a rebellion and this book just needs to decide what it is and to stop trying to be 4785478 things at once. It needs to cool its fucking jets. You want Wild West? Do Wild West. You want Arabic folklore, do it (properly). But those things mix like soy milk and boiling water. The political and social mechanics of the Wild West (the ungoverned fringes of a too-big empire, the ever-changing frontier, the unstructured infancy of a new country), make 0 sense when they're flopping around amongst the ancient, highly structured, and orderly world of old Arabia. <br /><br />It doesn't help that this book is written from the POV of a generic heroine with a generic backstory and a generic voice. Even the parts of this book that held promise (I guess the...scenery might have been cool? I'm a sad, needy bitch for anything set in the desert. I love the desert) are bogged down in mediocrity. I suppose I can see why this might be enjoyable: it could perhaps be one of those gems that lets you switch your brain off and just yield to the fluffy, silly fun of the story. Listen: I'm more than capable of doing that. I love fluff books. I'm a stan for <i>The Selection</i>, for crêpes' sake. But the problem is that this book is not fun or immersive, and it also depicts parental abuse, systemic oppression, rampant sexism, frequent rape threats, and a violent rebellion. That's...not really in the spirit of the fluff book, is it? <br /><br />If handled with nuance, these topics can and definitely should be depicted (I am not, for fuck's sake, going to even dignify the tangential argument of "depicting something isn't endorsing it!!!" because anyone who needs to be told that should be forced to mud-wrestle while wearing their most expensive clothing) but because they're included here, you can't argue that this is just meant to be a "silly book" or that we should lower our expectations. Come on, now. Let's be real here.<br /><br />This book was just a big dud for me. It's one of those books that I just can't wrap my head around, mostly because I just don't understand what it's trying to do or say or be. But beyond all of this, there's one thing that we always return to whenever we - <i>we</i> being my two-person book club - discuss this book. Guess what it is.<br /><br />If you guessed the gold suit, then you would be correct. <br /><br />The gold suit.<br /><br />the <br /><br />gold<br /><br />suit.<br /><br />Just don't even get me started on the guy in the gold suit. Don't even ask me about it. I just can't get over it. <br /><br />The gold suit.<br /><br /><b>THE SUIT WAS FUCKING GOLD AND THEN HE LEVELLED A TOWN.</b><br /><br />Bye.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7260029485757686042" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2048885992" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2048885992" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2048885992?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=western">western</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=war-setting">war-setting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magical-creatures">magical-creatures</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2048885992" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15221093664657683111">The series’ covers do not match! Why, oh why?<br/><br/>Tragedy aside, this shiny book took me longer than necessary to read. And it wasn’t because it wasn’t interesting, just very, very—pack of turtles running a marathon—slow. <br/><br/>The setting is unusual. It’s not everyday that I read a book set in the desert. That makes for a bleak visual world-building, I’m not going to lie. I wasn’t impressed by the description of places, no shock there. <br/><br/>Fortunately, I loved the mystical creatures presented, if I dare use t</span>
  <span id="freeText15221093664657683111" style="display:none">The series’ covers do not match! Why, oh why?<br /><br />Tragedy aside, this shiny book took me longer than necessary to read. And it wasn’t because it wasn’t interesting, just very, very—pack of turtles running a marathon—slow. <br /><br />The setting is unusual. It’s not everyday that I read a book set in the desert. That makes for a bleak visual world-building, I’m not going to lie. I wasn’t impressed by the description of places, no shock there. <br /><br />Fortunately, I loved the mystical creatures presented, if I dare use that word. Until we actually meet one of those creatures, they are talked about as if they were fairytale characters, like they may exist… somewhere. I had no idea this was the magic mentioned in the blurb. <br /><br />For a debut, it’s pretty well done. For a first in a new series, it’s not bad at all. It starts with action and ends with action. In between, however, it’s less Formula 1 and more Dora the Explorer. The danger is not as present and the walking and riding and escaping seem to be eternal. <br /><br />So thank goodness for a strong, three-dimensional and witty heroine to keep us company during this uncertain period of cat and mouse chase. There’s talk of a war… that’s on the brink of combustion somewhere… but we have to wait a long time before being privy to any juicy detail concerning it. Talk about building suspense. <br /><br />When I got to the end I couldn’t stop reading. The last 1/3 of the book is really something. It should have been like that all along in my opinion. The camaraderie and danger reminded me of the heist in Fast Five. Get the moneeeeeey. Get the poweeeeer. Do it. Do it. Dare to make a change. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15221093664657683111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_2048885992'><a id="like_count_review_2048885992" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/2048885992?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">150 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F24934065-rebel-of-the-sands">Like</a></span>

    <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk"><img alt="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597641717p2/66224803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2231660211?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk">Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2231660211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11483022852791696446"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1519315468ra/25105110.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i> "But if knowledge was power, then the unknown was the greatest weakness of immortal things.” </i><br/><br/>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/>Dustwalk always seemed like a prison to Amani - boring with horrible people in it. <br/>The only things she loved were her mother and shooting with a gun. <br/>When her mother gets hanged for killing her husband and Amani is being send to her aunt, Amani’s urge to run away becomes strong. <br/>She tries to win the money to get away - but chaos and a foreigner come into her way. <br/>Soon she meets the foreign</span>
  <span id="freeText11483022852791696446" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1519315468ra/25105110.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i> "But if knowledge was power, then the unknown was the greatest weakness of immortal things.” </i><br><br>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>Dustwalk always seemed like a prison to Amani - boring with horrible people in it. <br>The only things she loved were her mother and shooting with a gun. <br>When her mother gets hanged for killing her husband and Amani is being send to her aunt, Amani’s urge to run away becomes strong. <br>She tries to win the money to get away - but chaos and a foreigner come into her way. <br>Soon she meets the foreigner again and an exciting but dangerous adventure begins. <br>This book is full of great action, Djinns magic, stories and a rebellion with a traitor prince. <br>It has a good, nice pacing and some lovable characters. It’s definitely a book worth trying, let alone for the world building. <br>The book is also funny and feels magical, it makes you smile and dream of different wonderful worlds in it. 🎈<br><br>Characters ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>Amani is by far the coolest girl with a gun I know. She’s a badass and she knows that it’s completely stupid to think that women are less than man. <br>No, Amani knows she’s better than any man with a gun. She is strong, intelligent and sometimes ruthless. But in the end there are always secrets to discover. Even in yourself.<br><br><i> “(...) that girl who dressed as a Boy, who taught herself to shoot true, who dreamed and saved and wanted so badly. That girl was someone who had made herself matter.” </i> <br><br>And Jin, oh my wonderful Jin. Your smile makes empires turn on each other and girls go dumb. Your heart is full of kindness and love for the world. For your family and for the girl you love. <br>You thought Amani is a badass? Well you haven’t met Shazi yet, who appears a little later in the book. She’s a real fighter, a born soldier who knows strategy and skill like no one else. She’s definitely one of my favorite female characters now. <br><br>World ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>Just imagine you’re somewhere in the desert - maybe in Egypt or in the United Arabic Emirates. There’s desert, there’s gunpowder and there are soldiers everywhere. <br>You’re ruled by a Sultan, a ruthless man who decided some time ago, that he should rule Miraji instead of his father. So he partnered up with the Gallans - an enemy to Miraji - to kill his own family and get himself on the throne. But there’s a rebellion against him - led by his own son. <br>But there aren’t only humans in this world. When God created the world he created the First Beings - Djinn, Buraqi.. magical creatures that are powerful and connect with the sand and sun. <br>They lived undisturbed until the Destroyer of worlds came and twisted the world. They fought, but the First Beings never knew what death is until this day. So they created the Mortals who were brave, fought and died for them. <br>Soon the Destroyer of worlds was defeated, but he left something on earth for the mortals to fear. Ghouls and other creatures who can be the death of you. Sometimes they’re called nightmares and they suck the life out of you until your soul is gone. <br>But the immortals didn’t disappear. They stayed and sometimes loved humans. Soon there were children - half Djinn, half humans - Demdji who were gifted with Djinn powers. They create illusions only you can see, they can change their shape and their faces. They change into other people or even animals. They can become fire, death and sand. <br><br>Relationships ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>Is there anything sweeter than two people who found each other and learned that together they could survive this terrible world and actually change something? <br>There are passionate kisses to hide from the enemy and jokes on the long days together through the sand. <br><br>Writing style ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>It was a nice enjoyable writing with action, friendship, betrayal and love. It was filled with stories from Djinns and Mortals, ruthless Sultans and Princes that wish for a rebellion.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1519315589ra/25105112.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Great BR with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/70806774-ronak-pihu-gajjar" rel="nofollow noopener">my cutie :*</a></span>

<div id="review_1565980943" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1565980943" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1565980943?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780451477538" href="/book/show/25776221-rebel-of-the-sands">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1565980943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17375572633880905011"><blockquote>
  <i>❝Tell me that and we’ll go. Right now. Save ourselves and leave this place to burn. Tell me that’s how you want your story to go and we’ll write it straight across the sand.❞</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I think everything from <i>Rebel of the Sands</i> was set differently but it just made it! Alwyn Hamilton was able to mix fantasy with some romance in it and set it in a midwestern/eastern setting and I think that was great of her! Even with that, the fantasy added more since there were mythical creatures and abilities given to</span>
  <span id="freeText17375572633880905011" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>❝Tell me that and we’ll go. Right now. Save ourselves and leave this place to burn. Tell me that’s how you want your story to go and we’ll write it straight across the sand.❞</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I think everything from <i>Rebel of the Sands</i> was set differently but it just made it! Alwyn Hamilton was able to mix fantasy with some romance in it and set it in a midwestern/eastern setting and I think that was great of her! Even with that, the fantasy added more since there were mythical creatures and abilities given to the people. It was a great mix to read about and nothing was dull, boring, or unpleasant. Instead, everything was captivating since page 1 and everything just keep me going straight to the last page wanting book 2 already.<br /><br /><i>Rebel of the Sands takes place in Dustwalk, a place where women either get went or end up dead. So, they're known either to be married or to be shot by maybe the prince himself. Women are known as householders, orphans, poor, and of course, females. Amani Al’Hiza is all, with some special ability to herself. She's got a perfect aim for shooting and is able to take down anyone who gets in her way. She decides to dress as a boy and cover most of her face to show her eyes at least, but to her the rest of the feminine parts. As she entered this competition, what she really wants is the money that way she's able to leave this town she despises and go to Izman, a place where her mother would always tell her about and would encourage her to go. Now that she has a chance, she doesn't think about wasting it and needs to find a way to make it.<br /><br />In the competition, she meets a guy around her age named Jin, a foreigner who is also entered for the money. As she notices he's got good aim as a shooter and as she finds out he is headed out of Dustwalk as well, Amani wants nothing but to go with him and join him on his journey. But even though Jin isn't really headed to Izman but somewhere else than this ugly and poor town, Amani just wants freedom and to escape. Thinking Jin is her only escape and the only one able to help him, they decide to team up and escape where they are headed to.<br /><br />While being together and having moments together, Amani discovers secrets behind this town, about herself, and truths about each other.</i><br /><br />These are actually the kind of fantasy novels I enjoy flying through! It's set differently than others in a way. It started off with Amani being a string female lead and just to talk about her, I think her character was different than other YA female protagonists. Alwyn was able to create one who starts off strong but slowly fades. I think it was a good idea of her to release secrets and truths towards the end because of who Amani is and wished to be. Most of the time, women or young girls start off in a weak state. They grow by training and having more experience, ending up able to beat the guys in a competition involving guns, knives, climbing, fighting, defending and other fighting agilities. <br /><br />Amani was quite the same like other female characters, but at the same time she had her own character development. Finding out things afterwards made her realize other things and she realized she's been living a life she never thought about. It was different than what I expected. I didn't predict the ending or thinking think about it, and I didn't expect any of the middle, towards the end, or anything that was about to happen as I was turning the page. I was actually glad I didn't since the story was actually really cool and everything sort of went in it's own direction, making me enjoy it more. <br /><br />The foreigner, Jin, was actually always there to help Amani. Both had feelings for each other and I was glad the romance wasn't slow burn, fast paced or any of the romance had such suspense to it and leaved me shocked. Of course when I ship two characters together and am able to see them together, I get happy when there is a moment of them <b>together</b> but even with that, they both had their secrets to be told, truths to be discovered, and lies to be hidden as the two were on this journey together. He was able to help Amani with his sarcastic attitude and funny personality even when it came to being serious. He knew what he was doing and was able to do it in the right way.<br /><br />Everything was quick and since this turned out to be a trilogy, I was glad nothing ended in a way to leave me very bothered and wishing I never finished the story. Everything was such a cool experience and was glad there were elements added to it. From disguises to gun shootings. From mythical creatures to Nightmares actually being revealed. From pity to passion. I think it was great knowing Amani didn't like her town but then was able to discover things about it and realize her hatred for it should've been changed a long time ago. Even with all the side characters and other main characters, there weren't any who completely bothered me. There were reasons for the happenings and I'm pretty sure that in the other novels, we'll hear more about them. <br /><br />Overall, Rebel of the Sands was a great 2016 read and I'm looking forward for the rest of the trilogy. I don't really know who this would be a recommendation to, as in "fans of ___ will enjoy this" but I do recommend this to anyone who is a fan of fantasy novels. Fantasy overall would be the best genre to describe it since there is fantasy added to it all as the journey continues. I'm looking forward for the next installment and can't wait to see how Hamilton out stands everything else once again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17375572633880905011" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1355779981" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1355779981" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1355779981?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=magical-fantasy">magical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1355779981" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9495423677392197961">I get <i>slightly</i> nervous going into Massively Highly Anticipated Books of My Life -- because what if I don't like it???? What if my expectations are too high??? Whatifwhatifwhatif. But, WHY DID I EVEN WORRY ABOUT REBEL OF THE SANDS?!? <b>It was a glorious conglomeration of Persian fantasy, magic horses, sass, and guns...and I absolutely freaking loved it.</b><br/><br/>(Seriously tho, was this book written for me?? Omg.)<br/><br/><b>It's basically set in a dusty fantasy world with Middle Eastern influences.</b> I was actually surpr</span>
  <span id="freeText9495423677392197961" style="display:none">I get <i>slightly</i> nervous going into Massively Highly Anticipated Books of My Life -- because what if I don't like it???? What if my expectations are too high??? Whatifwhatifwhatif. But, WHY DID I EVEN WORRY ABOUT REBEL OF THE SANDS?!? <b>It was a glorious conglomeration of Persian fantasy, magic horses, sass, and guns...and I absolutely freaking loved it.</b><br /><br />(Seriously tho, was this book written for me?? Omg.)<br /><br /><b>It's basically set in a dusty fantasy world with Middle Eastern influences.</b> I was actually surprised because I NEVER read modern fantasy like this??? (It reminded me a bit of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9917938.Blood_Red_Road__Dust_Lands___1_" title="Blood Red Road (Dust Lands, #1) by Moira Young" rel="nofollow noopener">Blood Red Road</a> actually, which I also abso-freaking-lutely love.) We have, like, weapons factories and GUNNNNNNS and shooting people -- but we also have spirits and ghouls and terrible things lurking in the desert that like to rip your face off. #nice And sand. MUCH SAND. It actually almost had a <b>cowboy western</b> feel to it at times...but that could be because I just finished reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22501055.Under_a_Painted_Sky" title="Under a Painted Sky by Stacey Lee" rel="nofollow noopener">Under a Painted Sky</a> and am thinking of all the western things. AHEM. MOVING FORWARD!<br /><br /><b>Amani is downright awesome.</b> She's the "tough heroine" who is a wicked good shot and dreams of running away from her abusive relatives to FIND HER DESTINY OF AWESOME. But she's not ever irritating??? She's really <i>really</i> sassy. And she makes mistakes. Omg, so. many. mistakes. (I kind of wanted to hurt her when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ she left her BEST FRIEND in the dust to die while she ran away <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>..I mean, wut even Amani?!?!?) But she had <b>amazing character development</b> too. <br /><br />And of course there's the love interest: <b>Jin</b>. Whom I adored. It could be because of the sass. Or that he slinks into a shooting game in the local tavern and competes against Amani and they're <i>so stinkin' cute together</i>. Ooooor, it could be because he gets shot right at the front and I do love a good story where everyone is bleeding. Ahem.<br /><br />DID I MENTION THE SASS?!?! &lt;3<br /><br />Also the story itself?! <b>I basically loved it to absolute pieces.</b> It's fast! It's like this entire WORLD crammed into a 330 page novel and, um, hello and excuse me but I'M SO PLEASED ABOUT THIS. Usually I find smaller novels suck with the world building. BUT NOPE. Epic world building. Epic mythology. Epic settings. EEEEPIC EVERYTHING, DANGIT. (Although it did have a tendency to info-dump in the form of folklore tales occasionally. Which I'll forgive it for? But I wasn't particularly interested in those tales.)<br /><br />"So why isn't it full 5 stars, Cait?" you say, because you are intelligent and noticed I'm holding back. <i>Just slightly.</i> There were a smattering of things I found underwhelming. <br /><br /><b>For Instance:</b><br />• I predicted one of the biggest plot twists. I think it was waaaay too obvious. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I mean they said right up front all the legends of the Sultin's rebel prince and blah blah...I KNEW JIN HAD SOMETHING TO DO WITH IT. I don't know if there were too many hints? Or perhaps it was just too obvious? But <i>of course</i> Jin was brother to the famous rebel prince, ergo a prince himself, and saboteur of the weapons factory. I kind of rolled my eyes at that reveal, tbh. I saw it from page, like, 10. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />• Then I did get a bit confused at the end because there are SO MANY CHARACTERS and I'm still not 100% who is killing who and for what.<br />• Also Amani was way more spunky and awesome at the beginning. Maybe she was maturing? But as soon as Amani stopped shooting things along the journey, I was sad.<br />• I also saw the phrase "sharp shooter" in the blurb? And I thought that meant, like, taking out people at long distance or whatnot. But Amani was an AWESOME SHOT but she really wasn't hired for her gun or anything?<br />• It's very sexist. Like, that's okay! Because Amani was like kicking the sexism in the teeth...but I <i>am so tired</i> of sexist fantasy worlds.<br /><br /><br />...but basically?!? <b>This book was AMAZING and I want to hug it for nearly ever.</b> I'm so happy because of the Persian culture particularly (!! my favourite !!) and all the shooting and trains and MAGIC STUFF and wild actiony adventure. This is definitely on my "you must read it or I will perhaps growl" list. SO WHAT EVEN ARE YOU WAITING FOR??? GO GO GO.<br /><br /><br />** FAVOURITE QUOTES:<br /><br /><blockquote>Jin was at my side..."Did you just shoot someone?"<br />"I got us hired, if that's what you're asking. And I only shot his glass."<br />Jin hooked one arm around my shoulder, leaning on me. "I knew I liked you, Bandit."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"You're going to get us both killed if you go off looking for this on your own, you know. And if I was going to die on account of you, I'd rather have done it weeks ago before I had to do all this walking."</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="9495423677392197961" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1568469088" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1568469088" />
    <a title="Trina (Between Chapters)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9323164-trina-between-chapters"><img alt="Trina (Between Chapters)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530495507p2/9323164.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1568469088?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trina (Between Chapters)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trina (Between Chapters)" href="/user/show/9323164-trina-between-chapters">Trina (Between Chapters)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780451477538" href="/book/show/25776221-rebel-of-the-sands">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1568469088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1235315084143646233">The summary of this book calls it a mash up of The Wild West and Arabian Nights (though it is not a retelling). I think that's pretty accurate in terms of the setting and feel. I do want to acknowledge that there are many negative stereotypes about Middle Eastern culture and the historical US West that are used here, but I don't think the author has ever lived in either region as far as I can tell. Although I ended up loving this story, I don't disagree with people who have questioned if it was </span>
  <span id="freeText1235315084143646233" style="display:none">The summary of this book calls it a mash up of The Wild West and Arabian Nights (though it is not a retelling). I think that's pretty accurate in terms of the setting and feel. I do want to acknowledge that there are many negative stereotypes about Middle Eastern culture and the historical US West that are used here, but I don't think the author has ever lived in either region as far as I can tell. Although I ended up loving this story, I don't disagree with people who have questioned if it was her story to tell and say the Middle Eastern influence was poorly researched. I have read a couple of own voices reviews that seem to be in conflict about the representation, and as I have no experience with the background it's hard for me to know what to think.<br /><br />While reading, I was very engaged and found the story and world interesting and enjoyable. I kept being surprised at how much I liked it. I loved the world-building. It felt familiar AND fantastical. The magical creatures were interesting. I loved the creation mythology. I loved the magic system.<br /><br />There isn't a ton about the main character, Amani, that stands out to me as something I loved, but there was nothing about her that I hated either. Jin on the other hand was a character I enjoyed from start to finish. I loved the dynamic between the two of them.<br /><br />The middle portion of this book has kind of a survivalist tone and I'm always a sucker for that. Two characters with conflicting motives having to work together to survive? SIGN ME UP! <br /><br />I loved the pacing. There was a part of the story right past halfway where the action lulls off and we start to learn more about new things. This is usually where my attention would take a nose dive. I was expecting to lose momentum here but then surprisingly, things were revealed in a way that kept my interest and propelled me on to the end! I particularly loved that some big things were revealed around 3/4 in because this gave us a little time to explore them and get excited for the next book without revealing too early, which can sometimes make me grow bored.<br /><br />I love <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Amani's power and everything about how it was revealed. I expected her to have some type of magic, but I wasn't expecting her to be a Demdji. When she was trying to figure out what her power was, I was really afraid it would be something like Noorsham's - control of fire. This is a power that has been done to death so when we find out that she can actually control sand, I was excited! It totally fits her character and the world and it's something fresh (to me at least). I love that her eyes were her only marker, and the iron of her guns kept her power at bay, which is why she never knew. It was SO bittersweet to watch her gain this new power, but at the expense of her sharpshooter skill, which she taught herself, since using a gun essentially "turns off" her Demdji ability.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I loved that there were many villains, and I especially loved how one of them (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Noorsham <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>) is kind of a wildcard who you want to be won over to the good side but you can't tell how it will play out! I am so invested in seeing what happens with this one character! And the conflict they present to Amani! Ugh! My emotions were all over the place.<br /><br />This book took the overdone rebellion-trying-to-overthrow-an-evil-overlord trope and made me interested in it! I will definitely continue the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1235315084143646233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1316404338" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1316404338" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500935920p2/8472395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1316404338?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780451477538" href="/book/show/25776221-rebel-of-the-sands">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8472395-alyssa?shelf=2016-releases">2016-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1316404338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16353590207643103244">THE ENDING WAS PERFECT. Perfect, as in an excellent balance of "happy" and "omg tell me more". No cliffhanger, no agony, but things are just starting to heat up in the desert (hehehe). I can't wait to read more! :D<br/><br/><br/>***<a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2016/01/review-rebel-of-sands-by-alwyn-hamilton.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br/><br/>Rebel of the Sands by Alwyn Hamilton<br/>Book One of the Rebel of the Sands series<br/>Publisher: Penguin<br/>Publication Date: March 8, 2016<br/>Rating: 5 stars<br/>Source: ARC sent by the publisher<br/><br/>Summary (from Goodreads):<br/><br/>She’s more gunpowder than girl—and the f</span>
  <span id="freeText16353590207643103244" style="display:none">THE ENDING WAS PERFECT. Perfect, as in an excellent balance of "happy" and "omg tell me more". No cliffhanger, no agony, but things are just starting to heat up in the desert (hehehe). I can't wait to read more! :D<br /><br /><br />***<a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2016/01/review-rebel-of-sands-by-alwyn-hamilton.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br /><br />Rebel of the Sands by Alwyn Hamilton<br />Book One of the Rebel of the Sands series<br />Publisher: Penguin<br />Publication Date: March 8, 2016<br />Rating: 5 stars<br />Source: ARC sent by the publisher<br /><br />Summary (from Goodreads):<br /><br />She’s more gunpowder than girl—and the fate of the desert lies in her hands.<br /><br />Mortals rule the desert nation of Miraji, but mystical beasts still roam the wild and barren wastes, and rumor has it that somewhere, djinni still practice their magic. But there's nothing mystical or magical about Dustwalk, the dead-end town that Amani can't wait to escape from. <br /><br />Destined to wind up "wed or dead," Amani’s counting on her sharpshooting skills to get her out of Dustwalk. When she meets Jin, a mysterious and devastatingly handsome foreigner, in a shooting contest, she figures he’s the perfect escape route. But in all her years spent dreaming of leaving home, she never imagined she'd gallop away on a mythical horse, fleeing the murderous Sultan's army, with a fugitive who's wanted for treason. And she'd never have predicted she'd fall in love with him...or that he'd help her unlock the powerful truth of who she really is.<br /><br />What I Liked:<br /><br />Ahhh, I can see why this book has received so many stunningly positive early reviews so far, and why it's set to be a huge success worldwide. This book was magical! And such a fun, exciting fantasy novel. So many YA fantasy books today are so heavy and gloom-and-doom-y, save-the-world-and-claim-the-throne kinds. This book has certain elements that are typical of YA fantasy novels, but nothing like your average YA fantasy, in my opinion.<br /><br />Amani desperately wants to escape the small desert town of Dustwalk. She's excellent with a gun, and she's hoping to use those skills to win some prize money and get out of the town, before her uncle marries her off. With a little help from a handsome foreigner, Amani escapes into the world outside of Dustwalk. But she isn't expecting the wild adventure that follows, tangling her up in rebellion and revolution and magic she has never seen before. <br /><br />My expectations have been super high, ever since seeing this book's cover (the original one AND the new one!). It's not always smart to be excited about a book solely based on the cover, but in this case, I was justified. Kickbutt fantasy + amazing synopsis + gorgeous cover? This book has been calling to me! So I'm even more excited that it did not disappoint, because my expectations were crazy high!<br /><br />Amani surprised me from the very beginning. I know we in the YA book world like to throw around phrases like "kicka** heroine", how some heroines are tough and feisty and spunky and whatnot. But Amani is a different kind of tough. She's so incredibly mouthy, and she stands in the face of danger and does not back down. I love her wild spirit, and how unafraid she is to show her temper's claws. Not that she has an angry temper - but her personality is very fiery. I love her to pieces! Her character development was a very important part of this book; as she matures as she discovers the world beyond Dustwalk.<br /><br />The world-building of this book is incredible! Desert fantasies are nothing new in YA, but this desert fantasy is a little different. Guns and trains and other technology totally exist, and yet, so does Djinni and ghouls and magic. The world is also highly patriarchal, and polygamy is very common. Amani's uncle has many wives who all live together with their children... it's just of awful to read, and a bit heartbreaking. The Sultan himself has, and I quote, "more sons than there are hours in the day" (ARC, 170). While no one will like this polygamous aspect (I hope!), everyone can agree that its presence helps the authenticity and richness of the world-building.<br /><br />Did I mention how much I liked the setting? No? I love desert settings. I like how the author made this desert setting very unique and almost modern, but totally not modern. We're not stuck in Dustwalk for very long, and Amani travels through many places. This book takes place over many months (at least two), and I like how the pacing felt. <br /><br />Our male protagonist is Jin, who is the foreigner mentioned in the synopsis. Jin! Ah! I liked him a lot. He's charming and funny and adept in a fight. He's handsome and muscular and extremely intelligent. We don't know exactly who he is for a good part of the book, but when we find out, it came as a bit of a surprise to me. I LOVE that the author does not take a cliche route with Jin. Jin is one of my favorite characters in the book, and I was cheering him on just as much as I was cheering on Amani.<br /><br />We meet many of our secondary characters in the latter half of the book, and I adore so many of them! Shazad is another strong female, in a different way. Hala too. Bahi is such a sweetie! I love the twins too. The author does an excellent with the development of the secondary characters - and what a lovely cast of characters they were.<br /><br />The story captivated me, and I love how the author moved the plot. The book never seemed slow, or overwhelming. This book is the first in a trilogy, so the author did not get into the heavier parts of the fantasy in this particular book. We are introduced to the political conflicts and there are some key moves made in this book. But I liked that, despite all of that, this story remained fun and adventurous. I'm sure it'll get more calculating and threatening and fearful in the next two books, but I'm savoring the adventure that was this first book.<br /><br />There is a subtle and sweet romance in this book! The synopsis alludes to it, and I'm happy to say that I love the blossoming relationship between Amani and Jin. I LOVE that they are slowly coming to understand their feelings - there are no "I love you"'s thrown around, and no one is making rash decisions for the sake of each other. The romance is so sweet, and yet, so sneaky. I foresee more swoony scenes in future books, but this one kept the romance light and sweet. Also, no love triangle in any way shape or form! Not an insinuation or speck or whiff.<br /><br />No cliffhanger either! Small mercy there, because I have been hit with so many cliffhangers recently. Phew! I'm sure there will be a cliffhanger at the end of book two of the trilogy (as it usually happens), but we're safe for now!<br /><br />Have I said enough to convince you? I'm going to wrap up my review a little, because I could probably go on and on. I loved this beautiful story and cannot wait to read the next book!<br /><br />What I Did Not Like:<br /><br />Nothing that I can think of at the moment! Maybe that we have to wait for the sequel?! Personal request there - more kissing!<br /><br />Would I Recommend It:<br /><br />Whether you're a YA fantasy fan or not, this is definitely NOT a book to miss. The ending is not cliffhanger-y at all, so it wouldn't hurt to start now! I so want to reread this book and experience it all over again. What a fabulous story!<br /><br />Rating:<br /><br />4.5 stars -&gt; rounded up to 5 stars. I can see this being a favorite at the end of the year! I don't give the five-star rating often, but I'm thinking this book deserves it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16353590207643103244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
